**Plan.md Alignment**
- **Phase 0 Preparation**: terminology/tasks captured, but the snapshot/ignore work is still open (Plan §0 “Snapshot current state”; .live-documentation isn’t ignored yet).
- **Phase 1 – Schema & Instructions**: largely complete; only the “Evidence links updated once lower layers refreshed” checkbox remains.
- **Phase 2 – Generator Foundations**: generator CLI, deterministic provenance, staging directory, and lint hooks are implemented; diff tooling/migration strategy is still pending.
- **Phase 3 – Evidence & Coverage Bridges**: coverage manifest + evidence injection and integration smoke tests (`tests/integration/live-docs/*.ts`) exist, but waiver enforcement and benchmark wiring called out in Plan §3/§7 (“waiver lint warns”, “benchmarks confirm ≥0.9/≥0.8”) aren’t wired yet.
- **Phases 4–7** (CLI parity, docstring drift, migration, enrichers) remain untouched; they’re still unchecked in live-documentation-doc-refactor-plan.md.

**Commit-Ready Gaps**
- Generated artefacts (`.live-documentation/**`, targets.json) are appearing in `git status`; we need ignore rules or guidance before the tree is “stable”.
- Waiver workflow, docstring drift, and CLI parity work from Plan Phases 3–5 are outstanding, so the new tooling is more prototype than “more capable than last commit”.
- Integration relies on compiled server assets (`packages/server/dist/...`); we haven’t proven the build/test cycle yet with `npm run verify`/`safe:commit`, nor updated documentation (Plan §5) to describe runtime expectations for the extension and CLI consumers.

**Next Steps**
1. Add ignore rules and finish Plan §0 snapshot so generated mirrors stop polluting status while we iterate.
2. Finish the remaining Phase 3 items (waiver lint + precision benchmarks) and document Layer 4 archetype expectations per Plan §5 before calling the branch commit-ready.
3. Schedule work for Phase 4+ (CLI/diagnostic parity, docstring drift enforcement) so we can demonstrate the new stack delivers the “more capable” bar spelled out in the plan.

Made changes.

jfjordanfarr: A-ha! Unfinished business! Do you recall what I said about this block yesterday? About whether or not we should include that block in the emitted markdown Live Documentation files? We no doubt need to _know_ about the presence of absence of test coverage, but we would prefer for the "Observed Evidence" block to be an **optional** populated field in the Generated section of a LIve Documentation file. The reason I say this is because that Observed Evidence section is just a glorified "find all references" but for specifically tests. I think that it's really valuable for a fair number of cases, but I also think that it takes up a very large amount of text real estate in these generated docs. Therefore, I would prefer to keep it _optional_ whether or not the "Observed Evidence" block is **written** to the markdown files. Is that possible for us to do, or does that request to make it optional make the actual process of linting very very hard? (We're tryinig to build very good AST-based validations using Markdown links, and I can fully understand why the absence of the actual _written_ markdown links to the test evidence could make our job of verifying it potentially needlessly difficult )

And beyond all of that, there was a genuine difficult contention we wanted to resolve about whether we wanted to ignore the pattern we'd established of dependency tracking directionality by having a Generated markdown section containing _inbound_ links. We wanted our Live Documentation files for our Tests to note the (Live Documentation link) for the units they test. Here's a good example from the currently-existing generated #file:environment.test.ts.mdmd.md :
````markdown

- Code Path: packages/server/src/runtime/environment.test.ts
````

Given that we _do_ have a record of which "implementation" archetype Live Documentation files are being targeted by any given "test" archetype Live Documentation file, should we:
- Stop emitting the "Observed Evidence" block and continue the pattern of having each Live Documentation file only worry bout its public symbols and dependencies, OR
- Optionally allow the redundant "Observed Evidence" generated block, but not rely on it for... lint...checks? 

Overall I think that (under the hood) we should retain the pattern of every Live Documentation file worrying only about its dependencies and public symbols, but I can also see the value of immediately _feeling_ whether or not a Live Documentation file of "implementation" archetype has been sufficiently covered with testing at a glance. 

What do you think?

GitHub Copilot: - You’re right to flag the sprawl: forcing “Observed Evidence” into every implementation doc bloats the markdown and duplicates what the targets manifest already captures. We can keep the evidence snapshot metadata in memory (and surface it through the CLI/diagnostics), but only render the block when there’s something useful to show or when a waiver explicitly asks for it.
- Concretely, I’ll update the generator so implementations include `Observed Evidence` only when:
  - there are concrete references/coverage entries to display, or
  - a waiver is recorded and should be surfaced (with a short, structured entry).
  In all other cases we’ll skip the block entirely. This preserves the AST-friendly links when they exist while avoiding giant empty sections and redundant data.
- On the lint side, we’ll loosen the requirement from “must have Observed Evidence” to “if the section exists, validate it; otherwise rely on the generator’s metadata to ensure the manifest is up to date.” That keeps waivers enforceable without penalising terse docs.
- For tests, we’ll keep the `Targets` block—they’re the inbound links you want, and they let us reason about coverage without needing the reverse listing. To control noise, we can collapse long target lists into suite headers (only emit one bullet per suite + count unless `--verbose` is requested).
- Net result: generated docs stay lean, lints still guard waivers/coverage when present, and the data remains available to tooling. I’ll start by adjusting the generator and lint script to follow this strategy unless you’d prefer the alternative (always emit but hide behind a `--include-evidence` flag).

jfjordanfarr: > - Concretely, I’ll update the generator so implementations include `Observed Evidence` only when:
>  - there are concrete references/coverage entries to display, or
>  - a waiver is recorded and should be surfaced (with a short, structured entry).
>  In all other cases we’ll skip the block entirely. This preserves the AST-friendly links when they exist while avoiding giant empty sections and redundant data.

Overall that sounds good, but which markdown links would you use? Would you link, in "Observed Evidence", to the real test files or to the Live Documentation equivalent of them? The Live Docuementation equivalent has (much) shorter relative paths to traverse, but is less directly and obviously verifiable. Still, I believe that I would prefer for Live Documentation files to only link directly to source code that _they own_, and all other links should be to other Live Documentation docs and symbols. If we can pull that off without totally bloating our logic, I'm down.

GitHub Copilot: Summarized conversation history

jfjordanfarr: You just came out of a lossy autosummarization step. Please rehydrate on today's dev day chat history so far and then proceed with answering my latest question:
#file:2025-11-09.md:1-605 

GitHub Copilot: Read [](file:///d%3A/Projects/Copilot-Improvement-Experiments/AI-Agent-Workspace/ChatHistory/2025-11-09.md#1-1), lines 1 to 401

Linking the Observed Evidence row items to the test Live Docs is the cleaner fit for the rules we’ve been following. That keeps every outbound link inside an implementation doc pointed either at the source file it owns or at another Live Doc/symbol, preserves the short relative paths, and still lets the tooling trace back to the underlying `.ts` via the evidence manifest. To make that work I’ll:

- emit the Observed Evidence block only when we actually have evidence rows or a waiver, as discussed;
- build each bullet as a link to the test’s Layer‑4 Live Doc (e.g. `../../../../tests/.../foo.test.ts.mdmd.md`) with the readable test filename as the label;
- keep the raw file paths and symbol data in the JSON manifest so precision checks and CLI inspections can continue to reason about real code locations.

That way the markdown stays lean and AST-friendly, while the diagnostics still have access to the “real” targets when they need deeper validation. Let me know if you’d like me to sneak in the raw file path—maybe in a title attribute or via an optional verbose mode—but defaulting to Live Doc links hits the intent you outlined. Next up: I’ll adjust the generator and lint pipeline to implement that conditional rendering and link shape.

**Latest Update**
- Tried to filter the integration suite to the “Rapid markdown edits” scenario, but the harness has no file-level filtering, so the full suite executed again.
- Suite outcome flipped: US1 debounce case passed this time, while T053 latency telemetry failed (`Expected p95 <= 3375ms, received 3616ms`). That 3375ms limit is the Windows tolerance (base 2500ms × 1.35).
- No new code edits; only observed the rerun logs and inspected diagnosticLatency.test.ts to confirm how tolerance is computed.

**Key Takeaways**
- US1 regression looks flaky rather than a persistent failure—likely worth keeping an eye on but not currently blocking.
- Telemetry latency is now the primary blocker. We need to determine whether the slowdown is environmental noise or a genuine regression caused by the Live Docs changes.

**Next Steps**
1. Re-run T053 (or the whole suite) to confirm the latency overrun is reproducible and gather more telemetry samples.
2. If reproducible, add temporary logging around `linkDiagnostics.getLatencySummary` to capture `thresholdMs`, `p95LatencyMs`, and sample counts for diagnosis.
3. Depending on findings, either tune the extension performance (preferred) or, if evidence shows a consistent baseline shift, revisit the tolerance constant.

Made changes.

jfjordanfarr: How did `pathUtils.js.mdmd.md` come to exist? That almost sounds like the auto-generator picked up some intermediary file and put down a doc for it. Do we have a mechanism to detect orphans? Live Documentation files for which no corresponding code files exist?

GitHub Copilot: pathUtils.js.mdmd.md comes straight from a real file: we check in both pathUtils.ts and its CommonJS companion pathUtils.js. The live-doc generator sweeps everything under `packages/**` that matches our tracked extensions (`.ts`, `.js`, etc.), so it dutifully mirrors the CJS build output as well. It isn’t a transient artifact—it’s there so consumers that still require `require()` can import the helper without a compile step.

We don’t yet have an automated prune for “doc without source” in the current toolchain. If someone deletes the code file but leaves the live doc, regeneration won’t remove it automatically; you’d still see the orphan until we clean it up by hand. A linter check to flag missing `Code Path` targets is on the backlog, but it isn’t wired in today. For now the best safeguard is awareness during refactors (and, in a pinch, a quick `findstr`/`ripgrep` to confirm the referenced source still exists).

jfjordanfarr: I know that we're very close to completing the list of remaining manual documentation items, so I just wanted to make sure that we've got our eyes looking ahead for when we want to take off the gitignore on `.live-documentation/` and begin using it as our primary source of documentation (with an understanding that we will likely need future commits to transform/migrate equivalents for MDMD layers 1-3; there remain open design questions on what the Generated versus Authored portions of those should be, and how they could be plausibly derived).

Made changes.

jfjordanfarr: Hey can we chat about this `mdmd.layer4.asset.instructions.md` file? This was introduced by you yesterday and I think it violates the patterns that we've been designing for Live Documentation, at least with respect to the order of finding dependencies. Recall that earlier in this conversation, we resolved to remove or optionalize the "Observed Evidence" section from the standard "implementation" archetype Live Documentation files, as it amounted to a sophisticated pre-baked find-all references. We wanted to stick to relying on our tooling to help us determine _inbound_ links to Live Documentation files by programmatically traversing the "Public Symbols" and "Dependencies" that each Live Documentation file knows about itself. This keeps our architecture smart and clean.

But for binary/non-plaintext assets, a place where an archetype was already hesitantly agreed to by me in the first place (in place of a direct markdown link to the binary/non-plaintext asset itself), the instructions are telling us to state the "Dependencies" as consumers _of_ the asset. Indeed, the "Consumers" proposed section below it is much the same but for ostensibly other Live Documentation files. That is not how this should work. To begin with, an "asset" archetype live documentation file (as in, a member of the Base Layer of Live Documentation) already can only have its public symbols and dependencies written in via manual authorship, as we would have no automated tooling to detect it (and most cases would have no such relationships anyway). We should tell our future selves reading this instructions file far in the future that these instructions are _just_ for manual authorship of the file, and that for the _vast majority_ of binary/non-plaintext files, there should not be any need for an asset type Live Documentation file, and a direct markdown link to the asset itself from "implementation" or "test" archetype Base Layer Live Documentation files should suffice as a means to account for all salient interdependent source files. 

GitHub Copilot: Read [](file:///d%3A/Projects/Copilot-Improvement-Experiments/.github/instructions/mdmd.layer4.asset.instructions.md)

Read [](file:///d%3A/Projects/Copilot-Improvement-Experiments/.github/instructions/instructions.instructions.md)

Using "Apply Patch"


```

```
Updated mdmd.layer4.asset.instructions.md to match the live-doc design we discussed: asset docs are now framed as rare, manually-authored exceptions; generated sections stop after `Public Symbols` and `Dependencies`; those dependencies describe only what the asset itself consumes, never downstream consumers; and guidance now prefers direct links whenever possible. Let me know if you want any further tweaks or examples baked into the instructions.
